Question: 5 horses are in a race. Mr.Jain selects two of horses at random and bets on them. The probability that he selected the winning horse is # Answer option: ['A)1/5', 'B)2/5', 'C)3/5', 'D)4/5', 'E)6/5']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the probability that Mr. Jain selects the winning horse when he randomly selects two horses out of the five.

1. **Total number of ways to select two horses from five:**
The number of ways to choose 2 horses out of 5 is given by the combination formula \( \binom{n}{r} \), where \( n \) is the total number of items to choose from, and \( r \) is the number of items to choose. So, we have:
\[
\binom{5}{2} = \frac{5 \times 4}{2 \times 1} = 10
\]

2. **Number of favorable outcomes:**
For Mr. Jain to have selected the winning horse, the winning horse must be one of the two horses he selects. There is only 1 winning horse in the race. Once the winning horse is selected, Mr. Jain can choose any of the remaining 4 horses to complete his selection of two horses. Therefore, the number of favorable outcomes is the number of ways to choose 1 horse from the remaining 4 horses:
\[
\binom{4}{1} = 4
\]

3. **Probability calculation:**
The probability that Mr. Jain selects the winning horse is the number of favorable outcomes divided by the total number of outcomes:
\[
\text{Probability} = \frac{\text{Number of favorable outcomes}}{\text{Total number of outcomes}} = \frac{4}{10} = \frac{2}{5}
\]

Thus, the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse is \(\frac{2}{5}\).

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: Silu and Meenu were walking on the road. Silu said, "I weigh 51 Kgs. How much do you weigh?" Meenu replied that she wouldn't reveal her weight directly as she is overweight. But she said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight. "How much does Meenu weigh? # Answer option: ['A)12', 'B)28', 'C)27', 'D)58', 'E)91']
To solve the problem, we need to determine Meenu's weight based on the information she provided.

Meenu said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight." Let's denote Meenu's weight as \( x \).

According to her statement, we can set up the equation:
\[ x = 29 + \frac{x}{2} \]

To solve for \( x \), we first eliminate the fraction by multiplying the entire equation by 2:
\[ 2x = 58 + x \]

Next, we subtract \( x \) from both sides to isolate \( x \) on one side of the equation:
\[ 2x - x = 58 \]
\[ x = 58 \]

Therefore, Meenu weighs 58 Kgs.

Now, let's verify the answer with the given options:
- A) 12
- B) 28
- C) 27
- D) 58
- E) 91

The correct answer is option D) 58.

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: Three bells ring at intervals of 36 seconds, 40 seconds and 48 seconds, respectively. They start ringing together at a particular time. When they will ring together again? # Answer option: ['A)After 6 minutes', 'B)After 12 minutes', 'C)After 18 minutes', 'D)After 24 minutes', 'E)none']
To determine when the three bells will ring together again, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of their ringing intervals: 36 seconds, 40 seconds, and 48 seconds.

**Step 1: Prime Factorization**
- 36 = 2^2 * 3^2
- 40 = 2^3 * 5
- 48 = 2^4 * 3

**Step 2: Determine the LCM**
The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime number that appears in the factorizations:

- The highest power of 2 is 2^4 (from 48).
- The highest power of 3 is 3^2 (from 36).
- The highest power of 5 is 5 (from 40).

Thus, the LCM = 2^4 * 3^2 * 5.

**Step 3: Calculate the LCM**
- 2^4 = 16
- 3^2 = 9
- 5 = 5

Now, multiply these together:
- 16 * 9 = 144
- 144 * 5 = 720

The LCM of 36, 40, and 48 is 720 seconds.

**Step 4: Convert Seconds to Minutes**
720 seconds is equal to 720 / 60 = 12 minutes.

Therefore, the three bells will ring together again after 12 minutes.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: A box contains a certain number of balls, marked successively from 1 to n. If there are 45 different ways that two balls can be selected from the box such that the ball with number 3 marked on it is not selected, then what is the value of n? # Answer option: ['A)11', 'B)10', 'C)9', 'D)8', 'E)7']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the total number of balls, \( n \), in the box such that there are 45 different ways to select two balls without selecting the ball marked with the number 3.

First, let's consider the total number of balls, \( n \). If we exclude the ball marked with the number 3, we have \( n - 1 \) balls remaining.

The number of ways to choose 2 balls from \( n - 1 \) balls is given by the combination formula:

\[
\binom{n-1}{2} = \frac{(n-1)(n-2)}{2}
\]

We are given that this number of combinations is 45:

\[
\frac{(n-1)(n-2)}{2} = 45
\]

To solve for \( n \), we first multiply both sides by 2 to eliminate the fraction:

\[
(n-1)(n-2) = 90
\]

Next, we expand the left side:

\[
n^2 - 3n + 2 = 90
\]

Subtract 90 from both sides to set the equation to zero:

\[
n^2 - 3n + 2 - 90 = 0
\]

\[
n^2 - 3n - 88 = 0
\]

Now, we solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula, where \( a = 1 \), \( b = -3 \), and \( c = -88 \):

\[
n = \frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}
\]

\[
n = \frac{-(-3) \pm \sqrt{(-3)^2 - 4 \cdot 1 \cdot (-88)}}{2 \cdot 1}
\]

\[
n = \frac{3 \pm \sqrt{9 + 352}}{2}
\]

\[
n = \frac{3 \pm \sqrt{361}}{2}
\]

\[
n = \frac{3 \pm 19}{2}
\]

This gives us two potential solutions for \( n \):

\[
n = \frac{3 + 19}{2} = 11
\]

\[
n = \frac{3 - 19}{2} = -8
\]

Since \( n \) must be a positive integer, we discard \( n = -8 \) and accept \( n = 11 \).

Thus, the value of \( n \) is 11.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: x men working x hours per day can do x units of a work in x days. How much work can be completed by y men working y hours per day in y days? # Answer option: ['A)x2/y2 units', 'B)y3/x2 units', 'C)x3/y2 units', 'D)y2/x2 units', 'E)None of these']
To solve this problem, we need to understand the relationship between the number of men, the number of hours they work per day, the number of days they work, and the amount of work they can complete.

Given:
- \( x \) men working \( x \) hours per day can complete \( x \) units of work in \( x \) days.

From this, we can deduce the total amount of work done in terms of man-hours:
- Total man-hours required to complete \( x \) units of work = \( x \) men \(\times\) \( x \) hours/day \(\times\) \( x \) days = \( x^3 \) man-hours.

Now, we need to find out how much work \( y \) men working \( y \) hours per day can complete in \( y \) days.

The total man-hours available with \( y \) men working \( y \) hours per day for \( y \) days is:
- Total man-hours available = \( y \) men \(\times\) \( y \) hours/day \(\times\) \( y \) days = \( y^3 \) man-hours.

Since \( x^3 \) man-hours are required to complete \( x \) units of work, the amount of work that can be completed with \( y^3 \) man-hours is proportional to the ratio of \( y^3 \) to \( x^3 \).

The work completed by \( y \) men in \( y \) days working \( y \) hours per day is:
- Work completed = \( x \) units \(\times\) \(\frac{y^3}{x^3}\).

Now, let's simplify this expression:
- Work completed = \(\frac{y^3}{x^3} \times x = \frac{y^3 \times x}{x^3} = \frac{y^3}{x^2}\).

Thus, the amount of work that can be completed by \( y \) men working \( y \) hours per day in \( y \) days is \(\frac{y^3}{x^2}\) units.

Therefore, the correct answer is option B.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ? # Answer option: ['A)226', 'B)230', 'C)240', 'D)260', 'E)280']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the minimum selling price per component that will ensure a yearly profit of at least $626,400.

1. **Calculate the Total Yearly Production Cost:**
- The company produces 420 units per month.
- The production cost per component is $110.
- Total production cost per month = 420 units * $110/unit = $46,200.
- Total production cost per year = $46,200/month * 12 months = $554,400.

2. **Determine the Required Yearly Revenue:**
- The desired yearly profit is $626,400.
- Yearly profit = Yearly revenue - Yearly production cost.
- Therefore, Yearly revenue = Yearly profit + Yearly production cost.
- Yearly revenue = $626,400 + $554,400 = $1,080,800.

3. **Calculate the Minimum Selling Price per Component:**
- The company sells 420 units per month, so in a year, it sells 420 units/month * 12 months = 5,040 units.
- To find the minimum selling price per component, divide the required yearly revenue by the total number of units sold in a year.
- Minimum selling price per component = $1,080,800 / 5,040 units = $214.68.

4. **Choose the Minimum Selling Price from the Options:**
- The minimum selling price must be at least $214.68 to achieve the desired profit.
- From the given options, the smallest price that is greater than or equal to $214.68 is $226.

Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee the yearly profit is at least $626,400 is $226.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: One gram of a certain health food contains 9 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin E and 8 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin A. If vitamins E and A are to be obtained from no other source, how many grams of the health food must be eaten daily to provide at least the minimum daily requirement of both vitamins? # Answer option: ['A)8.5', 'B)10.5', 'C)12.5', 'D)14.5', 'E)16.5']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how many grams of the health food are required to meet at least 100% of the minimum daily requirement for both vitamin E and vitamin A.

1. **Vitamin E Requirement:**
- Each gram of the health food provides 9% of the daily requirement of vitamin E.
- To find out how many grams are needed to meet 100% of the requirement, we set up the equation:
\[
9\% \times \text{grams} = 100\%
\]
- Solving for grams:
\[
\text{grams} = \frac{100\%}{9\%} = \frac{100}{9} \approx 11.11
\]

2. **Vitamin A Requirement:**
- Each gram of the health food provides 8% of the daily requirement of vitamin A.
- To find out how many grams are needed to meet 100% of the requirement, we set up the equation:
\[
8\% \times \text{grams} = 100\%
\]
- Solving for grams:
\[
\text{grams} = \frac{100\%}{8\%} = \frac{100}{8} = 12.5
\]

3. **Determine the Maximum Requirement:**
- To satisfy both vitamin requirements, we need to take the maximum of the two calculated values because we need to meet at least 100% of both vitamins.
- The maximum of 11.11 grams (for vitamin E) and 12.5 grams (for vitamin A) is 12.5 grams.

Therefore, to meet at least the minimum daily requirement of both vitamins, one must consume at least 12.5 grams of the health food daily.

Final answer: {C}
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is # Answer option: ['A)4 1/3 km/h', 'B)7 2/3 km/h', 'C)9 ½ km/h', 'D)8 km/h', 'E)81 km/h']
To find the average speed, we need to calculate the total distance traveled and the total time taken, and then divide the total distance by the total time.

1. **Calculate the total distance:**
- Distance traveled at 5 km/h for 6 hours:
\[
\text{Distance} = \text{Speed} \times \text{Time} = 5 \, \text{km/h} \times 6 \, \text{h} = 30 \, \text{km}
\]
- Distance traveled at 4 km/h for 12 hours:
\[
\text{Distance} = \text{Speed} \times \text{Time} = 4 \, \text{km/h} \times 12 \, \text{h} = 48 \, \text{km}
\]

2. **Calculate the total distance:**
\[
\text{Total Distance} = 30 \, \text{km} + 48 \, \text{km} = 78 \, \text{km}
\]

3. **Calculate the total time:**
\[
\text{Total Time} = 6 \, \text{h} + 12 \, \text{h} = 18 \, \text{h}
\]

4. **Calculate the average speed:**
\[
\text{Average Speed} = \frac{\text{Total Distance}}{\text{Total Time}} = \frac{78 \, \text{km}}{18 \, \text{h}} = 4.3333 \, \text{km/h}
\]

5. **Convert the average speed to a fraction:**
\[
4.3333 \, \text{km/h} = 4 \frac{1}{3} \, \text{km/h}
\]

Therefore, the average speed is \(4 \frac{1}{3} \, \text{km/h}\).

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: If a man rows at the rate of 4 kmph in still water and his rate against the current is 2 kmph, then the man's rate along the current is: # Answer option: ['A)15 kmph', 'B)6 kmph', 'C)12 kmph', 'D)14 kmph', 'E)6 kmph']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the man's rate along the current. We are given two pieces of information:

1. The man's rowing rate in still water is 4 kmph.
2. The man's rate against the current is 2 kmph.

Let's denote:
- \( v_b \) as the man's rowing speed in still water (4 kmph).
- \( v_c \) as the speed of the current.
- \( v_{against} \) as the man's speed against the current (2 kmph).
- \( v_{along} \) as the man's speed along the current.

The man's speed against the current can be expressed as:
\[ v_{against} = v_b - v_c \]

Substituting the given values:
\[ 2 = 4 - v_c \]

Solving for \( v_c \):
\[ v_c = 4 - 2 = 2 \text{ kmph} \]

Now, we need to find the man's speed along the current, which can be expressed as:
\[ v_{along} = v_b + v_c \]

Substituting the known values:
\[ v_{along} = 4 + 2 = 6 \text{ kmph} \]

Therefore, the man's rate along the current is 6 kmph.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: At what price should the Karan mark a sewing machine that costs him Rs. 1200/- so that even after offering a 20% discount, he makes 20% profit? # Answer option: ['A)1,879', 'B)1,875', 'C)1,876', 'D)1,872', 'E)1,800']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the marked price of the sewing machine such that after offering a 20% discount, Karan still makes a 20% profit on the cost price.

1. **Determine the Selling Price for 20% Profit:**
- The cost price (CP) of the sewing machine is Rs. 1200.
- Karan wants to make a 20% profit on the cost price.
- Profit = 20% of CP = 0.20 * 1200 = Rs. 240.
- Therefore, the selling price (SP) should be CP + Profit = 1200 + 240 = Rs. 1440.

2. **Determine the Marked Price for a 20% Discount:**
- Let the marked price be \( M \).
- Karan offers a 20% discount on the marked price.
- The selling price after the discount is 80% of the marked price (since 100% - 20% = 80%).
- Therefore, 0.80 * M = 1440.

3. **Solve for the Marked Price:**
- \( M = \frac{1440}{0.80} \).
- \( M = 1800 \).

Thus, the marked price should be Rs. 1800 to achieve a 20% profit after offering a 20% discount.

Question: If 27 bottles of soda cost A cents, how much will B bottles cost in dollars? # Answer option: ['A)AB/2700', 'B)27/AB', 'C)AB/270', 'D)2700/AB', 'E)100AB/27']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the cost of B bottles of soda in dollars, given that 27 bottles cost A cents.

1. **Determine the cost of one bottle in cents:**
- If 27 bottles cost A cents, then the cost of one bottle is \( \frac{A}{27} \) cents.

2. **Determine the cost of B bottles in cents:**
- If one bottle costs \( \frac{A}{27} \) cents, then B bottles will cost \( B \times \frac{A}{27} = \frac{AB}{27} \) cents.

3. **Convert the cost from cents to dollars:**
- Since there are 100 cents in a dollar, to convert the cost from cents to dollars, we divide by 100.
- Therefore, the cost of B bottles in dollars is \( \frac{AB}{27} \div 100 = \frac{AB}{2700} \).

Thus, the cost of B bottles in dollars is \( \frac{AB}{2700} \).

Question: The difference between simple interest and C.I. at the same rate for Rs.5000 for 2 years in Rs.72. The rate of interest is? # Answer option: ['A)10%', 'B)12%', 'C)6%', 'D)8%', 'E)4%']
To solve this problem, we need to find the rate of interest at which the difference between the compound interest (C.I.) and simple interest (S.I.) for Rs. 5000 over 2 years is Rs. 72.

Let's denote:
- Principal (P) = Rs. 5000
- Time (T) = 2 years
- Rate of interest (R) = unknown

The formula for simple interest is:
\[ \text{S.I.} = \frac{P \times R \times T}{100} \]

The formula for compound interest is:
\[ \text{C.I.} = P \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^T - P \]

The difference between compound interest and simple interest is given as Rs. 72:
\[ \text{C.I.} - \text{S.I.} = 72 \]

Substituting the formulas, we have:
\[ P \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - P - \frac{P \times R \times T}{100} = 72 \]

Substitute \( P = 5000 \) and \( T = 2 \):
\[ 5000 \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - 5000 - \frac{5000 \times R \times 2}{100} = 72 \]

Simplify:
\[ 5000 \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - 5000 - 100R = 72 \]

Divide the entire equation by 5000 to simplify:
\[ \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - 1 - \frac{100R}{5000} = \frac{72}{5000} \]

\[ \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - 1 - \frac{R}{50} = 0.0144 \]

Expand the square:
\[ \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 = 1 + \frac{2R}{100} + \frac{R^2}{10000} \]

Substitute back:
\[ 1 + \frac{2R}{100} + \frac{R^2}{10000} - 1 - \frac{R}{50} = 0.0144 \]

Simplify:
\[ \frac{2R}{100} + \frac{R^2}{10000} - \frac{R}{50} = 0.0144 \]

Combine terms:
\[ \frac{R^2}{10000} + \frac{R}{50} - \frac{R}{50} = 0.0144 \]

\[ \frac{R^2}{10000} = 0.0144 \]

Multiply through by 10000 to clear the fraction:
\[ R^2 = 144 \]

Take the square root of both sides:
\[ R = 12 \]

Thus, the rate of interest is 12%.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: John conducted a survey about car color. 60% of the people who took the survey were women. Of the men who were surveyed, 75% preferred red cars over green cars. If 10 men liked green cars more than red, how many people took the survey? # Answer option: ['A)100', 'B)120', 'C)50', 'D)200', 'E)80']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the total number of people who took the survey.

1. **Understand the given information:**
- 60% of the survey participants were women.
- 40% of the survey participants were men (since 100% - 60% = 40%).
- 75% of the men preferred red cars over green cars.
- 10 men preferred green cars over red cars.

2. **Calculate the number of men who preferred green cars:**
- If 75% of the men preferred red cars, then 25% of the men preferred green cars (since 100% - 75% = 25%).
- We know that 25% of the men equals 10 men (since 10 men preferred green cars).

3. **Calculate the total number of men:**
- Let \( x \) be the total number of men.
- 25% of \( x \) is equal to 10 men.
- Therefore, \( 0.25x = 10 \).
- Solving for \( x \), we get \( x = \frac{10}{0.25} = 40 \).

4. **Calculate the total number of people who took the survey:**
- Since 40% of the survey participants were men, and there are 40 men, we can set up the equation:
- Let \( y \) be the total number of people who took the survey.
- 40% of \( y \) is equal to 40 men.
- Therefore, \( 0.40y = 40 \).
- Solving for \( y \), we get \( y = \frac{40}{0.40} = 100 \).

Thus, the total number of people who took the survey is 100.

Final answer: {A}

Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: In a railway station, there are two trains going. One in the harbor line and one in the main line, each having a frequency of 10 minutes. The main line service starts at 5 o'clock and the harbor line starts at 5.02 A.M. A man goes to the station every day to catch the first train that comes. What is the probability of the man catching the first train? # Answer option: ['A)0.9', 'B)0.8', 'C)0.6', 'D)0.65', 'E)1.5']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the probability of the man catching the first train that arrives at the station. Let's break down the situation:

1. **Train Schedules:**
- The main line train arrives every 10 minutes starting at 5:00 A.M. So, the main line train arrives at 5:00, 5:10, 5:20, 5:30, etc.
- The harbor line train arrives every 10 minutes starting at 5:02 A.M. So, the harbor line train arrives at 5:02, 5:12, 5:22, 5:32, etc.

2. **Time Intervals:**
- From 5:00 to 5:02, the main line train is the first to arrive.
- From 5:02 to 5:10, the harbor line train is the first to arrive.
- From 5:10 to 5:12, the main line train is the first to arrive.
- From 5:12 to 5:20, the harbor line train is the first to arrive.
- This pattern repeats every 10 minutes.

3. **Probability Calculation:**
- In each 10-minute cycle, the main line train is the first to arrive for 2 minutes (from 5:00 to 5:02 and from 5:10 to 5:12).
- The harbor line train is the first to arrive for 8 minutes (from 5:02 to 5:10 and from 5:12 to 5:20).

4. **Probability of Catching the First Train:**
- The probability that the man catches the main line train (first train) is the ratio of the time intervals when the main line train is the first to arrive to the total time interval.
- Probability = (Time interval for main line train being first) / (Total time interval)
- Probability = 2 minutes / 10 minutes = 0.2

Therefore, the probability of the man catching the first train (main line train) is 0.2.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B? # Answer option: ['A)180', 'B)90', 'C)270', 'D)360', 'E)None of the above']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the distance between points A and B based on the information given about Kevin's trip.

1. **Understanding the Problem:**
- Kevin drives from A to B at 70 mph.
- He returns from B to A at 90 mph.
- 3 hours before the end of his trip, he is 70 miles away from B, still approaching it.

2. **Analyzing the Return Trip:**
- Since Kevin is 70 miles away from B and still approaching it 3 hours before the end of his trip, he must be on his way to B at that point.
- He is traveling at 70 mph towards B, so in 1 hour, he would cover 70 miles, reaching B.

3. **Time Calculation:**
- Since he is 70 miles away from B and traveling at 70 mph, it takes him 1 hour to reach B.
- After reaching B, he immediately turns around and heads back to A.
- The total time from the point he is 70 miles away from B to the end of his trip is 3 hours.
- Therefore, after reaching B, he has 2 hours left to complete his trip back to A.

4. **Distance Calculation:**
- In the 2 hours after reaching B, Kevin travels back to A at 90 mph.
- Distance covered in 2 hours at 90 mph = 90 mph * 2 hours = 180 miles.

5. **Distance Between A and B:**
- Since the distance from B to A is 180 miles, the distance from A to B is also 180 miles (as the distance is the same in both directions).

Therefore, the distance between A and B is 180 miles.

Final answer: {A}

Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: The telephone bill of a certain establishment is party fixed and partly varies as the number of calls consumed. When in a certain month 540 calls made the bill is Rs.1800. In another month 620 calls are consumed then the bill becomes Rs.2040. In another month 500 units are consumed due to more holidays. The bill for that month would be : # Answer option: ['A)Rs.1560', 'B)Rs.1680', 'C)Rs.1840', 'D)Rs.1950', 'E)Rs.1690']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the fixed and variable components of the telephone bill.

Let's denote:
- \( F \) as the fixed part of the bill.
- \( V \) as the variable cost per call.

From the problem, we have two scenarios:

1. For 540 calls, the bill is Rs.1800:
\[
F + 540V = 1800
\]

2. For 620 calls, the bill is Rs.2040:
\[
F + 620V = 2040
\]

We have two equations:
1. \( F + 540V = 1800 \)
2. \( F + 620V = 2040 \)

To find \( V \), we subtract the first equation from the second:
\[
(F + 620V) - (F + 540V) = 2040 - 1800
\]
\[
620V - 540V = 240
\]
\[
80V = 240
\]
\[
V = \frac{240}{80} = 3
\]

Now that we have \( V = 3 \), we can substitute it back into one of the original equations to find \( F \). Using the first equation:
\[
F + 540 \times 3 = 1800
\]
\[
F + 1620 = 1800
\]
\[
F = 1800 - 1620 = 180
\]

Now we have:
- Fixed cost \( F = 180 \)
- Variable cost per call \( V = 3 \)

For a month with 500 calls, the bill would be:
\[
F + 500V = 180 + 500 \times 3
\]
\[
= 180 + 1500
\]
\[
= 1680
\]

Therefore, the bill for the month with 500 calls is Rs.1680.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another? # Answer option: ['A)1 hr 23 min', 'B)1 hr 15 min', 'C)1 hr 8 min', 'D)56 min', 'E)55 min']
To solve this problem, we need to determine when the two trains cross each other. Let's break down the information given:

1. Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am. Therefore, the travel time for Train M is 4 hours.

2. Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am. Therefore, the travel time for Train N is 3.5 hours.

Next, we need to calculate the speeds of the trains. Since the distance between City A and City B is the same for both trains, we can use the formula:

\[ \text{Speed} = \frac{\text{Distance}}{\text{Time}} \]

Let's assume the distance between City A and City B is \( D \).

- Speed of Train M = \( \frac{D}{4} \)
- Speed of Train N = \( \frac{D}{3.5} = \frac{2D}{7} \)

Now, we need to find the time at which the two trains meet. Train M starts at 5 am, and Train N starts at 7 am. Therefore, by the time Train N starts, Train M has already been traveling for 2 hours.

In 2 hours, Train M covers a distance of:

\[ \text{Distance covered by Train M in 2 hours} = 2 \times \frac{D}{4} = \frac{D}{2} \]

This means that when Train N starts at 7 am, Train M has already covered half the distance between City A and City B.

Now, the remaining distance for both trains to meet is \( \frac{D}{2} \).

The relative speed of the two trains when they are moving towards each other is the sum of their speeds:

\[ \text{Relative speed} = \frac{D}{4} + \frac{2D}{7} = \frac{7D}{28} + \frac{8D}{28} = \frac{15D}{28} \]

The time taken for the trains to meet is given by:

\[ \text{Time} = \frac{\text{Distance}}{\text{Relative Speed}} = \frac{\frac{D}{2}}{\frac{15D}{28}} = \frac{D}{2} \times \frac{28}{15D} = \frac{28}{30} = \frac{14}{15} \text{ hours} \]

Convert \(\frac{14}{15}\) hours into minutes:

\[ \frac{14}{15} \times 60 = 56 \text{ minutes} \]

Therefore, the two trains will meet 56 minutes after 7 am, which is at 7:56 am.

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: If Q, a positive integer, has 5 factors, which of the following must be true about Q? I. Q is the square of a prime number. II. Q is the fourth power of a prime number. III. Q is the product of two prime numbers. # Answer option: ['A)I only', 'B)III only', 'C)II only', 'D)I and II only', 'E)I and III only']
To determine which statements must be true about a positive integer \( Q \) that has exactly 5 factors, we need to analyze the possible forms of \( Q \).

The number of factors of a positive integer \( n \) with the prime factorization \( n = p_1^{a_1} \times p_2^{a_2} \times \ldots \times p_k^{a_k} \) is given by the formula:

\[
(a_1 + 1)(a_2 + 1) \ldots (a_k + 1)
\]

For \( Q \) to have exactly 5 factors, the product of the increments of the exponents must equal 5. Since 5 is a prime number, the only way to achieve this is if one of the increments is 5 and all others are 1. This implies that \( Q \) must be of the form \( p^4 \), where \( p \) is a prime number.

Now, let's evaluate each statement:

I. **Q is the square of a prime number.**

If \( Q = p^2 \), then the number of factors would be \( (2 + 1) = 3 \), which is not 5. Therefore, this statement is false.

II. **Q is the fourth power of a prime number.**

If \( Q = p^4 \), then the number of factors would be \( (4 + 1) = 5 \). This matches the condition given in the problem. Therefore, this statement is true.

III. **Q is the product of two prime numbers.**

If \( Q = p_1 \times p_2 \), where \( p_1 \) and \( p_2 \) are distinct primes, then the number of factors would be \( (1 + 1)(1 + 1) = 4 \), which is not 5. Therefore, this statement is false.

Based on the analysis, only statement II is true. Therefore, the correct answer is:

Final answer: {C}

Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work? # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)8', 'C)22', 'D)50', 'E)20']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how long it takes Jill to finish the remaining work on the yacht.

1. **Determine Jack's rate of work:**
- Jack can clean the entire yacht in 12 hours. Therefore, his rate of work is \( \frac{1}{12} \) of the yacht per hour.

2. **Calculate the work Jack has already done:**
- Jack finishes two-thirds of the work. Therefore, the work he has completed is \( \frac{2}{3} \) of the yacht.

3. **Determine the remaining work:**
- The remaining work is \( 1 - \frac{2}{3} = \frac{1}{3} \) of the yacht.

4. **Determine Jill's rate of work:**
- Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of Jack's rate. Therefore, Jill's rate is \( 0.05 \times \frac{1}{12} = \frac{1}{240} \) of the yacht per hour.

5. **Calculate the time it takes Jill to finish the remaining work:**
- Jill needs to complete \( \frac{1}{3} \) of the yacht. The time \( t \) it takes her to do this is given by the equation:
\[
\text{Work} = \text{Rate} \times \text{Time}
\]
\[
\frac{1}{3} = \frac{1}{240} \times t
\]
- Solving for \( t \), we multiply both sides by 240:
\[
t = 240 \times \frac{1}{3} = 80
\]

Therefore, it takes Jill 80 hours to finish the remaining work.

Question: Train A leaves a station every 16 minutes and Train B leaves every 17 minutes. If both trains just left the station simultaneously, how long until they do so again? # Answer option: ['A)272 minutes', 'B)304 minutes', 'C)190 minutes', 'D)70 minutes', 'E)35 minutes']
To determine when both trains will leave the station simultaneously again, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of the two departure intervals: 16 minutes for Train A and 17 minutes for Train B.

1. **Identify the numbers**: We have 16 and 17.

2. **Prime factorization**:
- 16 is \(2^4\).
- 17 is a prime number, so its prime factorization is \(17^1\).

3. **Calculate the LCM**:
- The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime number that appears in the factorizations.
- For 2, the highest power is \(2^4\).
- For 17, the highest power is \(17^1\).

4. **Multiply these together**:
\[
\text{LCM} = 2^4 \times 17^1 = 16 \times 17
\]

5. **Calculate the product**:
\[
16 \times 17 = 272
\]

Thus, the least common multiple of 16 and 17 is 272 minutes. This means both trains will leave the station simultaneously again after 272 minutes.

To determine what percent the astronaut's weight on Venus is of their weight on Earth, we can use the formula for percentage:

\[
\text{Percentage} = \left( \frac{\text{Weight on Venus}}{\text{Weight on Earth}} \right) \times 100
\]

Given:
- Weight on Earth = 211 pounds
- Weight on Venus = 182 pounds

Substitute these values into the formula:

\[
\text{Percentage} = \left( \frac{182}{211} \right) \times 100
\]

Now, calculate the fraction:

\[
\frac{182}{211} \approx 0.8626
\]

Convert this to a percentage:

\[
0.8626 \times 100 \approx 86.26\%
\]

Rounding 86.26% to the nearest whole number gives us 86%.

Therefore, the weight of the astronaut on Venus is approximately 86% of their weight on Earth.

Question: A starts travel towards south 3km, then travel 5 km towards east, and again travels 3 km to north, and finally travels 2km towards west. In the end how far from is A from home? # Answer option: ['A)3km', 'B)2km', 'C)4km', 'D)5km', 'E)6km']
To determine how far A is from the starting point, we can break down the movements step by step and calculate the net displacement.

1. **Initial Position:** Let's assume A starts at the origin point (0, 0).

2. **Travel South 3 km:**
- Moving south decreases the y-coordinate.
- New position: (0, -3).

3. **Travel East 5 km:**
- Moving east increases the x-coordinate.
- New position: (5, -3).

4. **Travel North 3 km:**
- Moving north increases the y-coordinate.
- New position: (5, 0).

5. **Travel West 2 km:**
- Moving west decreases the x-coordinate.
- New position: (3, 0).

Now, we need to calculate the distance from the final position (3, 0) back to the starting point (0, 0).

The distance can be calculated using the distance formula for two points \((x_1, y_1)\) and \((x_2, y_2)\):
\[
\text{Distance} = \sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}
\]

Substituting the coordinates:
\[
\text{Distance} = \sqrt{(3 - 0)^2 + (0 - 0)^2} = \sqrt{3^2 + 0^2} = \sqrt{9} = 3
\]

Therefore, A is 3 km away from the starting point.

To find the perimeter of a rectangle, we use the formula:

\[ \text{Perimeter} = 2 \times (\text{Length} + \text{Width}) \]

Given that the length of the rectangle is 8 centimeters and the width is 3 centimeters, we can substitute these values into the formula:

\[ \text{Perimeter} = 2 \times (8 \, \text{cm} + 3 \, \text{cm}) \]

First, calculate the sum inside the parentheses:

\[ 8 \, \text{cm} + 3 \, \text{cm} = 11 \, \text{cm} \]

Next, multiply this sum by 2 to find the perimeter:

\[ \text{Perimeter} = 2 \times 11 \, \text{cm} = 22 \, \text{cm} \]

Therefore, the perimeter of the rectangle is 22 centimeters.

Question: Suppose for any real number x, [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x. Let L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] and R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]. Then it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which # Answer option: ['A)L(x,y) = R(x,y)', 'B)L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y)', 'C)L(x,y) < R(x,y)', 'D)L(x,y) < R(x,y)', 'E)None']
To solve this problem, we need to analyze the expressions \( L(x, y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] \) and \( R(x, y) = [2x] + [2y] \) and determine if there are any conditions under which these expressions are equal or not equal for positive real numbers \( x \) and \( y \).

### Step-by-step Analysis:

1. **Understanding the Floor Function:**
- The floor function \([x]\) gives the greatest integer less than or equal to \( x \).
- For any real number \( x \), we can express it as \( x = n + f \) where \( n = [x] \) is an integer and \( 0 \leq f < 1 \) is the fractional part.

2. **Expression for \( L(x, y) \):**
- \( L(x, y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] \).
- Let \( x = a + u \) and \( y = b + v \) where \( a = [x] \), \( b = [y] \), \( 0 \leq u < 1 \), and \( 0 \leq v < 1 \).
- Then, \( x + y = (a + b) + (u + v) \).
- The floor of \( x + y \) is \([x + y] = a + b + [u + v]\).
- If \( u + v < 1 \), then \([u + v] = 0\).
- If \( u + v \geq 1 \), then \([u + v] = 1\).

3. **Expression for \( R(x, y) \):**
- \( R(x, y) = [2x] + [2y] \).
- \( 2x = 2a + 2u \) and \( 2y = 2b + 2v \).
- \([2x] = 2a + [2u]\) and \([2y] = 2b + [2v]\).
- \([2u]\) is 0 if \( 0 \leq u < 0.5 \) and 1 if \( 0.5 \leq u < 1 \).
- \([2v]\) is 0 if \( 0 \leq v < 0.5 \) and 1 if \( 0.5 \leq v < 1 \).

4. **Comparing \( L(x, y) \) and \( R(x, y) \):**
- \( L(x, y) = a + b + (a + b + [u + v]) = 2a + 2b + [u + v] \).
- \( R(x, y) = 2a + 2b + [2u] + [2v] \).

5. **Conditions for Equality:**
- For \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \), we need \([u + v] = [2u] + [2v]\).
- If \( u + v < 1 \), then \([u + v] = 0\).
- If both \( u < 0.5 \) and \( v < 0.5 \), then \([2u] = 0\) and \([2v] = 0\), so \( [2u] + [2v] = 0 \).
- If one of \( u \) or \( v \) is \(\geq 0.5\), then \([2u] + [2v] = 1\), which is not equal to \([u + v] = 0\).
- If \( u + v \geq 1 \), then \([u + v] = 1\).
- This requires that at least one of \( u \) or \( v \) is \(\geq 0.5\), making \([2u] + [2v] = 1\).

6. **Conclusion:**
- It is possible to find \( x \) and \( y \) such that \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \) by choosing \( u \) and \( v \) such that both are less than 0.5 or both are greater than or equal to 0.5.
- Therefore, it is not impossible to find such \( x \) and \( y \).

The correct answer is that it is not impossible to find \( x \) and \( y \) such that \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \). Therefore, the answer is not option A. The correct answer is that it is possible to find such \( x \) and \( y \), so the answer is not option B either.

To solve this problem, we need to determine how far Bill can travel on a windy day in 21 minutes, given that his speed is reduced by 4 mph from his normal speed.

1. **Determine Bill's speed on a windy day:**
- Bill's normal speed is 15 mph.
- On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph.
- Therefore, his speed on a windy day is \(15 - 4 = 11\) mph.

- There are 60 minutes in an hour.
- 21 minutes is equal to \(\frac{21}{60}\) hours.

3. **Calculate the distance traveled:**
- Distance is calculated using the formula: \(\text{Distance} = \text{Speed} \times \text{Time}\).
- Substitute the values: \(\text{Distance} = 11 \, \text{mph} \times \frac{21}{60} \, \text{hours}\).

Question: Amy is organizing her bookshelves and finds that she has 10 different types of books. She then codes each book with either a single letter or a pair of two different letters. If each type of book is uniquely represented by either a single letter or pair of letters, what is the smallest number of letters Amy will need to create the codes for all 10 types of books? (Assume the order of letters in a pair does not matter.) # Answer option: ['A)3', 'B)4', 'C)5', 'D)10', 'E)20']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the smallest number of letters required to create unique codes for 10 different types of books, using either a single letter or a pair of two different letters.

Let's break down the possibilities:

1. **Single Letter Codes:**
- If we use \( n \) different letters, we can create \( n \) unique single-letter codes.

2. **Pair of Letters Codes:**
- If we use \( n \) different letters, the number of unique pairs of two different letters is given by the combination formula \( \binom{n}{2} = \frac{n(n-1)}{2} \).

The total number of unique codes we can create using \( n \) letters is the sum of single-letter codes and pair-of-letters codes:
\[
n + \binom{n}{2} = n + \frac{n(n-1)}{2}
\]

We need this total to be at least 10, as there are 10 types of books.

Let's calculate this for different values of \( n \):

- **For \( n = 3 \):**
\[
3 + \binom{3}{2} = 3 + 3 = 6
\]
This is not enough, as we need at least 10.

- **For \( n = 4 \):**
\[
4 + \binom{4}{2} = 4 + 6 = 10
\]
This is exactly 10, which is sufficient.

- **For \( n = 5 \):**
\[
5 + \binom{5}{2} = 5 + 10 = 15
\]
This exceeds 10, but we are looking for the smallest \( n \).

Since \( n = 4 \) is the smallest number of letters that allows us to create at least 10 unique codes, the answer is 4.

Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought? # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)3', 'C)2', 'D)1', 'E)0']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the minimum number of copper coins the diver could have brought up to earn exactly $3.40, given that she earns 20 cents per copper coin and 25 cents per brass coin.

Let's denote:
- \( x \) as the number of copper coins.
- \( y \) as the number of brass coins.

The total earnings equation based on the coins is:
\[ 0.20x + 0.25y = 3.40 \]

To eliminate decimals, multiply the entire equation by 100:
\[ 20x + 25y = 340 \]

We need to find the minimum value of \( x \) (copper coins) such that the equation holds true with \( x \) and \( y \) being non-negative integers.

First, let's express \( y \) in terms of \( x \):
\[ 25y = 340 - 20x \]
\[ y = \frac{340 - 20x}{25} \]

For \( y \) to be an integer, \( 340 - 20x \) must be divisible by 25. Let's check the values of \( x \) starting from the smallest possible integer:

1. **\( x = 0 \):**
\[ y = \frac{340 - 20 \times 0}{25} = \frac{340}{25} = 13.6 \]
\( y \) is not an integer.

2. **\( x = 1 \):**
\[ y = \frac{340 - 20 \times 1}{25} = \frac{320}{25} = 12.8 \]
\( y \) is not an integer.

3. **\( x = 2 \):**
\[ y = \frac{340 - 20 \times 2}{25} = \frac{300}{25} = 12 \]
\( y \) is an integer.

Since \( y \) is an integer when \( x = 2 \), this is the minimum number of copper coins that satisfies the equation.

Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins she brought is 2.

Question: What is the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation x2 - 5x + k = 0 will have two real and distinct roots? # Answer option: ['A)9', 'B)7', 'C)3', 'D)8', 'E)12']
To determine the largest integral value of \( k \) for which the quadratic equation \( x^2 - 5x + k = 0 \) has two real and distinct roots, we need to consider the discriminant of the quadratic equation. The discriminant \( \Delta \) of a quadratic equation \( ax^2 + bx + c = 0 \) is given by:

\[
\Delta = b^2 - 4ac
\]

For the quadratic equation to have two real and distinct roots, the discriminant must be greater than zero:

\[
\Delta > 0
\]

In the given equation \( x^2 - 5x + k = 0 \), we have \( a = 1 \), \( b = -5 \), and \( c = k \). Substituting these values into the discriminant formula gives:

\[
\Delta = (-5)^2 - 4 \cdot 1 \cdot k = 25 - 4k
\]

We require:

\[
25 - 4k > 0
\]

Solving this inequality for \( k \):

\[
25 > 4k
\]

\[
\frac{25}{4} > k
\]

\[
k < 6.25
\]

Since \( k \) must be an integer, the largest integer less than 6.25 is 6. Therefore, the largest integral value of \( k \) for which the quadratic equation will have two real and distinct roots is 6.

Thus, the final answer is:

\[
\text{Final answer:} \{C\}
\]
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is: # Answer option: ['A)2.6m', 'B)3.9m', 'C)4m', 'D)4.2m', 'E)4.4m']
To solve this problem, we need to find the height of the room given the cost of papering the walls and the ratio of the height to the semi-perimeter.

Let's break down the problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the Ratio:**
- The ratio of the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is given as 2:5.
- Let the height of the room be \( h \).
- Let the semi-perimeter of the room be \( s \).
- According to the ratio, \( \frac{h}{s} = \frac{2}{5} \) or \( h = \frac{2}{5} \times s \).

2. **Cost of Papering the Walls:**
- The cost to paper the walls is Rs. 260.
- The paper is 50 cm wide, which is 0.5 meters.
- The cost of the paper is Rs. 2 per meter.
- Therefore, the total length of paper used is \( \frac{260}{2} = 130 \) meters.

3. **Calculating the Area Covered by the Paper:**
- The area covered by the paper is the length of the paper multiplied by its width.
- Area covered = \( 130 \times 0.5 = 65 \) square meters.

4. **Adjusting for Doors and Windows:**
- An area of 15 square meters is allowed for doors and windows.
- Therefore, the actual area of the walls to be papered is \( 65 + 15 = 80 \) square meters.

5. **Relating Area to Room Dimensions:**
- The area of the walls is given by the perimeter of the room multiplied by the height.
- Let the perimeter of the room be \( P \).
- The area of the walls is \( P \times h = 80 \).

6. **Using the Semi-Perimeter:**
- The semi-perimeter \( s = \frac{P}{2} \).
- Therefore, \( P = 2s \).

7. **Substituting the Ratio:**
- From the ratio, \( h = \frac{2}{5} \times s \).
- Substitute \( P = 2s \) into the area equation:
\[
2s \times \frac{2}{5} \times s = 80
\]
\[
\frac{4}{5} s^2 = 80
\]
\[
s^2 = 80 \times \frac{5}{4} = 100
\]
\[
s = 10
\]

8. **Finding the Height:**
- Using \( h = \frac{2}{5} \times s \):
\[
h = \frac{2}{5} \times 10 = 4
\]

Therefore, the height of the room is 4 meters.

Final answer: {C}
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number. # Answer option: ['A)1584', 'B)2520', 'C)1728', 'D)1656', 'E)None']
To solve this problem, let's denote the number as \( x \).

1. **Calculate the correct value:**
- The correct calculation should be \( \frac{7}{8} \times x \).

2. **Calculate the incorrect value:**
- The student calculated \( \frac{7}{18} \times x \).

3. **Set up the equation for the difference:**
- The difference between the correct and incorrect values is given as 770.
- Therefore, we have:
\[
\frac{7}{8}x - \frac{7}{18}x = 770
\]

4. **Simplify the equation:**
- Factor out \( \frac{7}{8}x - \frac{7}{18}x \):
\[
\frac{7}{8}x - \frac{7}{18}x = \left(\frac{7}{8} - \frac{7}{18}\right)x
\]
- Find a common denominator for the fractions:
\[
\frac{7}{8} = \frac{63}{72}, \quad \frac{7}{18} = \frac{28}{72}
\]
- Subtract the fractions:
\[
\frac{63}{72} - \frac{28}{72} = \frac{35}{72}
\]
- Substitute back into the equation:
\[
\frac{35}{72}x = 770
\]

5. **Solve for \( x \):**
- Multiply both sides by \( \frac{72}{35} \) to solve for \( x \):
\[
x = 770 \times \frac{72}{35}
\]
- Calculate:
\[
x = 770 \times \frac{72}{35} = 770 \times \frac{72}{35} = 22 \times 72 = 1584
\]

6. **Conclusion:**
- The number is 1584.

Final answer: \(\{A\}\)
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: Boomtown urban planners expect the city’s population to increase by 10% per year over the next two years. If that projection were to come true, the population two years from now would be exactly double the population of one year ago. Which of the following is closest to the percent population increase in Boomtown over the last year? # Answer option: ['A)20%', 'B)40%', 'C)50%', 'D)65%', 'E)75%']
To solve this problem, we need to understand the relationship between the population changes over the years.

Let's denote the population one year ago as \( P \).

According to the problem, the population is expected to increase by 10% per year over the next two years. Therefore, the population at the end of the first year (current population) would be:

\[ P_{\text{current}} = P \times 1.1 \]

The population at the end of the second year would be:

\[ P_{\text{2 years}} = P_{\text{current}} \times 1.1 = P \times 1.1 \times 1.1 = P \times 1.21 \]

We are told that the population two years from now would be exactly double the population of one year ago. Therefore, we have:

\[ P \times 1.21 = 2P \]

To find the population increase over the last year, we need to determine the current population in terms of the population one year ago. We know:

\[ P_{\text{current}} = P \times 1.1 \]

We need to find the percentage increase from the population one year ago to the current population. The percentage increase is given by:

\[ \text{Percentage Increase} = \left( \frac{P_{\text{current}} - P}{P} \right) \times 100\% \]

Substituting the expression for \( P_{\text{current}} \):

\[ \text{Percentage Increase} = \left( \frac{P \times 1.1 - P}{P} \right) \times 100\% \]

\[ = \left( \frac{0.1P}{P} \right) \times 100\% \]

\[ = 10\% \]

However, this is the increase for one year. We need to find the increase over the last year, which is the increase from the population one year ago to the current population. Since the population two years from now is double the population one year ago, the current population must have increased by a certain percentage to fit this condition.

Let's re-evaluate the condition:

\[ P \times 1.21 = 2P \]

This implies that the population one year ago was actually \( \frac{P}{1.21} \) if we consider the current population as \( P \).

Therefore, the population one year ago was:

\[ P_{\text{1 year ago}} = \frac{P}{1.21} \]

The current population is \( P \).

The percentage increase from one year ago to the current population is:

\[ \text{Percentage Increase} = \left( \frac{P - \frac{P}{1.21}}{\frac{P}{1.21}} \right) \times 100\% \]

\[ = \left( \frac{1.21P - P}{P} \right) \times 100\% \]

\[ = \left( \frac{0.21P}{P} \right) \times 100\% \]

\[ = 21\% \]

This is the percentage increase from one year ago to the current population. However, this does not match any of the given options. Let's re-evaluate the options and calculations.

The correct approach is to consider the population one year ago as \( \frac{P}{1.21} \) and the current population as \( P \).

The percentage increase from one year ago to the current population is:

\[ \text{Percentage Increase} = \left( \frac{P - \frac{P}{1.21}}{\frac{P}{1.21}} \right) \times 100\% \]

Question: A retailer sold an appliance for 40 percent above cost, which represented a gross profit of $20.00. For what price did the retailer sell the appliance? # Answer option: ['A)$27.30', 'B)$51.00', 'C)$63.00', 'D)$70.00', 'E)$91.00']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the selling price of the appliance based on the information given.

1. **Understand the relationship between cost, selling price, and profit:**
- Let \( C \) be the cost price of the appliance.
- The selling price is 40% above the cost price, so the selling price \( S \) can be expressed as:
\[
S = C + 0.4C = 1.4C
\]
- The gross profit is given as $20.00, which is the difference between the selling price and the cost price:
\[
S - C = 20
\]

2. **Set up the equation using the profit information:**
- From the profit equation, we have:
\[
1.4C - C = 20
\]
- Simplify the equation:
\[
0.4C = 20
\]

3. **Solve for the cost price \( C \):**
- Divide both sides by 0.4 to find \( C \):
\[
C = \frac{20}{0.4} = 50
\]

4. **Calculate the selling price \( S \):**
- Substitute \( C = 50 \) back into the equation for the selling price:
\[
S = 1.4 \times 50 = 70
\]

5. **Verify the solution:**
- The cost price is $50.00.
- The selling price is $70.00.
- The profit is \( 70 - 50 = 20 \), which matches the given profit.

Therefore, the retailer sold the appliance for \(\$70.00\).

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: An express electric train takes exact three seconds to enter tunnel which is 1 mile long. If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel ? # Answer option: ['A)43 seconds', 'B)39 seconds', 'C)20 seconds', 'D)33 seconds', 'E)55 seconds']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how long it takes for the entire train to pass through the tunnel.

1. **Determine the length of the train:**
- The train takes 3 seconds to enter the tunnel. During this time, the entire length of the train enters the tunnel.
- The speed of the train is 120 miles per hour. We need to convert this speed into miles per second to find out how far the train travels in 3 seconds.
- There are 3600 seconds in an hour, so the speed in miles per second is:
\[
\frac{120 \text{ miles/hour}}{3600 \text{ seconds/hour}} = \frac{1}{30} \text{ miles/second}
\]
- In 3 seconds, the train travels:
\[
3 \times \frac{1}{30} = \frac{3}{30} = \frac{1}{10} \text{ miles}
\]
- Therefore, the length of the train is \(\frac{1}{10}\) miles.

2. **Determine the total distance the train needs to travel to completely pass through the tunnel:**
- The train needs to travel its own length plus the length of the tunnel to completely pass through.
- The length of the tunnel is 1 mile, and the length of the train is \(\frac{1}{10}\) miles.
- Total distance to travel = \(1 + \frac{1}{10} = \frac{11}{10} = 1.1\) miles.

3. **Calculate the time to travel this distance:**
- The train travels at a speed of 120 miles per hour, which is \(\frac{1}{30}\) miles per second.
- Time taken to travel 1.1 miles is:
\[
\frac{1.1 \text{ miles}}{\frac{1}{30} \text{ miles/second}} = 1.1 \times 30 = 33 \text{ seconds}
\]

Therefore, the train will take 33 seconds to completely pass through the tunnel.

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers? # Answer option: ['A)(zy – 2x)/z', 'B)(zy – 2)/z', 'C)(zx – y)/(z – 2)', 'D)(zy – 2x)/(z -2)', 'E)(zy – x)/(z + 2)']
To solve this problem, we need to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers. Let's break it down step by step:

1. **Understand the given information:**
- The average of the highest score (H) and the lowest score (L) is \( x \). Therefore, we have:
\[
\frac{H + L}{2} = x \implies H + L = 2x
\]

2. **Average score for the entire class:**
- The average score for the entire class is \( y \), and there are \( z \) students. Therefore, the total sum of all scores is:
\[
zy
\]

3. **Sum of scores excluding the highest and lowest:**
- The sum of all scores is \( zy \).
- The sum of the highest and lowest scores is \( H + L = 2x \).
- Therefore, the sum of the scores excluding the highest and lowest is:
\[
zy - 2x
\]

4. **Number of students excluding the highest and lowest scorers:**
- Since there are \( z \) students in total, excluding the highest and lowest scorers, there are \( z - 2 \) students.

5. **Average score excluding the highest and lowest scorers:**
- The average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is the sum of the scores excluding the highest and lowest divided by the number of students excluding the highest and lowest:
\[
\frac{zy - 2x}{z - 2}
\]

Thus, the correct answer is:
\[
\text{Final answer:} \{D\}
\]
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: Jerry purchased a 1-year $5,000 bond that paid an annual interest rate of 12% compounded every six months. How much interest had this bond accrued at maturity? # Answer option: ['A)$5102', 'B)$618', 'C)$216', 'D)$202', 'E)$200']
To determine how much interest the bond accrued at maturity, we need to calculate the future value of the bond using the given interest rate and compounding frequency.

1. **Identify the principal amount (P):**
The principal amount is $5,000.

2. **Determine the annual interest rate (r):**
The annual interest rate is 12%.

3. **Determine the compounding frequency:**
The interest is compounded every six months, which means it is compounded twice a year.

4. **Calculate the interest rate per compounding period:**
Since the interest is compounded semi-annually, the interest rate per period is half of the annual rate:
\[
\text{Interest rate per period} = \frac{12\%}{2} = 6\% = 0.06
\]

5. **Determine the number of compounding periods (n):**
Since the bond is for 1 year and compounds semi-annually, there are 2 compounding periods in total.

6. **Use the future value formula for compound interest:**
The future value \( FV \) of the bond can be calculated using the formula:
\[
FV = P \times (1 + r/n)^{nt}
\]
where \( P \) is the principal, \( r \) is the annual interest rate, \( n \) is the number of compounding periods per year, and \( t \) is the time in years.

Plugging in the values:
\[
FV = 5000 \times (1 + 0.06)^2
\]

7. **Calculate the future value:**
\[
FV = 5000 \times (1.06)^2 = 5000 \times 1.1236 = 5618
\]

8. **Calculate the interest accrued:**
The interest accrued is the future value minus the principal:
\[
\text{Interest} = 5618 - 5000 = 618
\]

Therefore, the interest accrued at maturity is $618.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: The length of the ribbon was originally 30 cm. It was reduced in the ratio 5 : 3. What is its length now? # Answer option: ['A)18', 'B)30', 'C)6', 'D)15', 'E)12']
To solve this problem, we need to understand what it means to reduce the length of the ribbon in the ratio 5:3.

1. **Understanding the Ratio**: The ratio 5:3 means that for every 5 units of the original length, it is now reduced to 3 units.

2. **Original Length**: The original length of the ribbon is 30 cm.

3. **Setting Up the Proportion**: We can set up a proportion to find the new length. If the original length (5 parts) is 30 cm, we need to find the new length (3 parts).

\[
\frac{5}{3} = \frac{30}{x}
\]

Here, \( x \) is the new length of the ribbon.

4. **Solving the Proportion**: Cross-multiply to solve for \( x \).

\[
5x = 3 \times 30
\]

\[
5x = 90
\]

\[
x = \frac{90}{5}
\]

\[
x = 18
\]

5. **Conclusion**: The new length of the ribbon is 18 cm.

Therefore, the correct answer is option A) 18.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: 64 boys and 40 girls form a group for social work. During their membership drive, the same number of boys and girls joined the group. How many members does the group have now, if the ratio of boys to girls is 4:3? # Answer option: ['A)277', 'B)288', 'C)200', 'D)277', 'E)168']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how many boys and girls joined the group such that the final ratio of boys to girls is 4:3.

1. **Initial Group Composition:**
- Boys = 64
- Girls = 40

2. **Let the number of boys and girls who joined be \( x \).**

3. **New Composition:**
- Boys = 64 + \( x \)
- Girls = 40 + \( x \)

4. **Given Ratio:**
- The ratio of boys to girls is 4:3.

5. **Set up the equation for the ratio:**
\[
\frac{64 + x}{40 + x} = \frac{4}{3}
\]

6. **Cross-multiply to solve for \( x \):**
\[
3(64 + x) = 4(40 + x)
\]

7. **Expand both sides:**
\[
192 + 3x = 160 + 4x
\]

8. **Rearrange to solve for \( x \):**
\[
192 - 160 = 4x - 3x
\]
\[
32 = x
\]

9. **Calculate the new number of boys and girls:**
- New number of boys = 64 + 32 = 96
- New number of girls = 40 + 32 = 72

10. **Total number of members in the group:**
\[
96 + 72 = 168
\]

11. **Verify the ratio:**
- Ratio of boys to girls = \(\frac{96}{72} = \frac{4}{3}\), which is correct.

Thus, the total number of members in the group now is 168.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs? # Answer option: ['A)0.5', 'B)0.6', 'C)0.7', 'D)0.8', 'E)0.9']
To solve this problem, we need to use the concept of independent events and the formula for the probability of the union of two events.

Given:
- \( P(A) = 0.6 \)
- \( P(A \cup B) = 0.96 \)

Since events A and B are independent, the probability of both A and B occurring is given by:
\[ P(A \cap B) = P(A) \times P(B) \]

We also know the formula for the probability of the union of two events:
\[ P(A \cup B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A \cap B) \]

Substituting the given values into this formula, we have:
\[ 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 \times P(B)) \]

Simplifying the equation:
\[ 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6P(B) \]

Combine like terms:
\[ 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B)(1 - 0.6) \]
\[ 0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B) \]

Subtract 0.6 from both sides:
\[ 0.36 = 0.4P(B) \]

Divide both sides by 0.4 to solve for \( P(B) \):
\[ P(B) = \frac{0.36}{0.4} \]
\[ P(B) = 0.9 \]

Thus, the probability that event B occurs is 0.9.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: On a test the passing students had an average of 83, while the failing students had an average of 55. If the overall class average was 76, what percent of the class passed? # Answer option: ['A)44%', 'B)66%', 'C)68%', 'D)72%', 'E)75%']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the percentage of students who passed the test. We have the following information:

- The average score of passing students is 83.
- The average score of failing students is 55.
- The overall class average is 76.

Let's denote:
- \( p \) as the proportion of students who passed.
- \( f \) as the proportion of students who failed.

Since the total proportion must equal 1, we have:
\[ p + f = 1 \]
\[ f = 1 - p \]

The overall class average can be expressed as a weighted average of the passing and failing students' averages:
\[ 83p + 55f = 76 \]

Substitute \( f = 1 - p \) into the equation:
\[ 83p + 55(1 - p) = 76 \]

Simplify the equation:
\[ 83p + 55 - 55p = 76 \]
\[ 28p + 55 = 76 \]

Subtract 55 from both sides:
\[ 28p = 21 \]

Divide both sides by 28 to solve for \( p \):
\[ p = \frac{21}{28} \]
\[ p = \frac{3}{4} \]
\[ p = 0.75 \]

Thus, 75% of the class passed the test.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: In how many ways can a teacher in a kindergarten school arrange a group of 3 children (Susan, Tim and Zen) on 3 identical chairs in a straight line so that Susan is on the left of Tim? # Answer option: ['A)7', 'B)3', 'C)2', 'D)1', 'E)6']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of ways to arrange the three children (Susan, Tim, and Zen) on three identical chairs in a straight line, with the condition that Susan is to the left of Tim.

1. **Calculate the total number of arrangements without any restrictions:**

There are 3 children and 3 chairs, so the total number of ways to arrange the children is given by the factorial of the number of children:
\[
3! = 3 \times 2 \times 1 = 6
\]
So, there are 6 possible arrangements of the children.

2. **Identify the arrangements where Susan is to the left of Tim:**

For each arrangement of the three children, there is a corresponding arrangement where Susan is to the left of Tim and another where Tim is to the left of Susan. Therefore, half of the total arrangements will have Susan to the left of Tim.

Since there are 6 total arrangements, the number of arrangements where Susan is to the left of Tim is:
\[
\frac{6}{2} = 3
\]

3. **List the valid arrangements:**

To verify, let's list the possible arrangements and check which ones satisfy the condition:
- Susan, Tim, Zen (STZ)
- Susan, Zen, Tim (SZT)
- Zen, Susan, Tim (ZST)

These are the 3 arrangements where Susan is to the left of Tim.

Thus, the number of ways to arrange the children such that Susan is on the left of Tim is 3.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: The cross-section of a canal is shaped like a trapezium. If the canal is 10 m wide at the top and 6 m wide at the bottom and the area of cross-section is 640 square meters, the depth of cannel is? # Answer option: ['A)26', 'B)28', 'C)21', 'D)80', 'E)23']
To find the depth of the canal, we need to use the formula for the area of a trapezium (trapezoid):

\[ \text{Area} = \frac{1}{2} \times (\text{Base}_1 + \text{Base}_2) \times \text{Height} \]

In this problem:
- \(\text{Base}_1 = 10\) m (the top width of the canal)
- \(\text{Base}_2 = 6\) m (the bottom width of the canal)
- \(\text{Area} = 640\) square meters

We need to find the height, which is the depth of the canal.

Plug the known values into the formula:

\[ 640 = \frac{1}{2} \times (10 + 6) \times \text{Height} \]

Simplify the equation:

\[ 640 = \frac{1}{2} \times 16 \times \text{Height} \]

\[ 640 = 8 \times \text{Height} \]

Now, solve for the height:

\[ \text{Height} = \frac{640}{8} \]

\[ \text{Height} = 80 \]

Therefore, the depth of the canal is 80 meters.

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: Arjun and Sajal are friends, each has some money. If Arun gives $30 to Sajal, the Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun. But, if Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal. How much money does each have? # Answer option: ['A)62, 35', 'B)62, 34', 'C)34, 62', 'D)42, 62', 'E)62, 42']
To solve this problem, let's define the variables:

- Let \( A \) be the amount of money Arjun has.
- Let \( S \) be the amount of money Sajal has.

We have two conditions given in the problem:

1. If Arjun gives $30 to Sajal, then Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun.
2. If Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, then Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal.

Let's translate these conditions into equations:

### Condition 1:
If Arjun gives $30 to Sajal, Arjun will have \( A - 30 \) and Sajal will have \( S + 30 \). According to the condition, Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun:

\[
S + 30 = 2(A - 30)
\]

Simplifying this equation:

\[
S + 30 = 2A - 60
\]

\[
S = 2A - 90 \quad \text{(Equation 1)}
\]

### Condition 2:
If Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have \( A + 10 \) and Sajal will have \( S - 10 \). According to the condition, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal:

\[
A + 10 = 3(S - 10)
\]

Simplifying this equation:

\[
A + 10 = 3S - 30
\]

\[
A = 3S - 40 \quad \text{(Equation 2)}
\]

### Solving the Equations:
Now, we have two equations:

1. \( S = 2A - 90 \)
2. \( A = 3S - 40 \)

Substitute Equation 1 into Equation 2:

\[
A = 3(2A - 90) - 40
\]

\[
A = 6A - 270 - 40
\]

\[
A = 6A - 310
\]

\[
310 = 6A - A
\]

\[
310 = 5A
\]

\[
A = 62
\]

Now, substitute \( A = 62 \) back into Equation 1 to find \( S \):

\[
S = 2(62) - 90
\]

\[
S = 124 - 90
\]

\[
S = 34
\]

Thus, Arjun has $62 and Sajal has $34. Therefore, the correct answer is:

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: In a survey of students, each student selected from a list of 10 songs the 2 songs that the student liked best. If each song was selected 5 times, how many students were surveyed? # Answer option: ['A)96', 'B)48', 'C)32', 'D)25', 'E)18']
To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:

1. **Understanding the Problem:**
- There are 10 songs.
- Each student selects their 2 favorite songs.
- Each song is selected 5 times.

2. **Determine Total Selections:**
- Since each song is selected 5 times, and there are 10 songs, the total number of selections made by all students is:
\[
10 \text{ songs} \times 5 \text{ selections per song} = 50 \text{ total selections}
\]

3. **Relate Selections to Students:**
- Each student selects 2 songs.
- Let \( n \) be the number of students surveyed.
- Since each student makes 2 selections, the total number of selections is also:
\[
2n
\]

4. **Set Up the Equation:**
- The total number of selections from both perspectives (total selections and selections per student) must be equal:
\[
2n = 50
\]

5. **Solve for \( n \):**
- Divide both sides of the equation by 2 to find the number of students:
\[
n = \frac{50}{2} = 25
\]

Thus, the number of students surveyed is 25.

Final answer: {D}

Question: What is the greatest number of identical bouquets that can be made out of 28 white and 98 red tulips if no flowers are to be left out? (Two bouquets are identical whenever the number of red tulips in the two bouquets is equal and the number of white tulips in the two bouquets is equal.) # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)7', 'C)10', 'D)14', 'E)21']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the greatest number of identical bouquets that can be made using all 28 white tulips and 98 red tulips, with no flowers left over. This means we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of the two numbers, 28 and 98.

Step 1: Find the prime factorization of each number.

- The prime factorization of 28 is:
\[
28 = 2^2 \times 7
\]

- The prime factorization of 98 is:
\[
98 = 2 \times 7^2
\]

Step 2: Identify the common prime factors and their lowest powers.

- Both numbers have the prime factors 2 and 7.
- The lowest power of 2 common to both factorizations is \(2^1\).
- The lowest power of 7 common to both factorizations is \(7^1\).

Step 3: Calculate the GCD by multiplying these common factors.

\[
\text{GCD} = 2^1 \times 7^1 = 2 \times 7 = 14
\]

Therefore, the greatest number of identical bouquets that can be made is 14.

Question: Two numbers are said to be relatively prime if they share no common positive factors other than 1. Set S contains the set of integers from 1 to 1,000, inclusive. What is the probability that a number chosen from S is relatively prime to 1,000? # Answer option: ['A)5/7', 'B)3/5', 'C)4/7', 'D)2/5', 'E)2/7']
To determine the probability that a number chosen from the set \( S \) (which contains integers from 1 to 1,000) is relatively prime to 1,000, we need to find the number of integers in \( S \) that are relatively prime to 1,000 and divide that by the total number of integers in \( S \).

### Step 1: Prime Factorization of 1,000
First, we find the prime factorization of 1,000:
\[ 1,000 = 10^3 = (2 \times 5)^3 = 2^3 \times 5^3 \]

### Step 2: Euler's Totient Function
The Euler's Totient Function, \(\phi(n)\), gives the count of numbers up to \( n \) that are relatively prime to \( n \). For a number \( n = p_1^{k_1} \times p_2^{k_2} \times \ldots \times p_m^{k_m} \), the function is given by:
\[
\phi(n) = n \left(1 - \frac{1}{p_1}\right)\left(1 - \frac{1}{p_2}\right)\ldots\left(1 - \frac{1}{p_m}\right)
\]

Applying this to 1,000:
\[
\phi(1000) = 1000 \left(1 - \frac{1}{2}\right)\left(1 - \frac{1}{5}\right)
\]
\[
= 1000 \times \frac{1}{2} \times \frac{4}{5}
\]
\[
= 1000 \times \frac{2}{5}
\]
\[
= 400
\]

So, there are 400 numbers in the set \( S \) that are relatively prime to 1,000.

### Step 3: Calculate the Probability
The total number of integers in \( S \) is 1,000. Therefore, the probability that a randomly chosen number from \( S \) is relatively prime to 1,000 is:
\[
\frac{400}{1000} = \frac{2}{5}
\]

Thus, the probability that a number chosen from \( S \) is relatively prime to 1,000 is \(\frac{2}{5}\).

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: A point on the edge of a fan blade that is rotating in a plane 10 centimeters from the center of the fan. What is the distance traveled, in centimeters, by this point after 30 seconds when the fan runs at the rate of 300 revolutions per minutes? # Answer option: ['A)750pi', 'B)1500pi', 'C)1875pi', 'D)3000pi', 'E)7500pi']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the distance traveled by a point on the edge of a fan blade. The point is 10 centimeters from the center of the fan, and the fan is rotating at a rate of 300 revolutions per minute.

1. **Calculate the circumference of the circle traced by the point:**
- The radius of the circle is 10 centimeters.
- The formula for the circumference \( C \) of a circle is \( C = 2\pi r \), where \( r \) is the radius.
- So, \( C = 2\pi \times 10 = 20\pi \) centimeters.

2. **Determine the number of revolutions in 30 seconds:**
- The fan rotates at 300 revolutions per minute.
- There are 60 seconds in a minute, so the fan makes \( \frac{300}{60} = 5 \) revolutions per second.
- In 30 seconds, the number of revolutions is \( 5 \times 30 = 150 \) revolutions.

3. **Calculate the total distance traveled by the point:**
- The distance traveled in one revolution is the circumference of the circle, which is \( 20\pi \) centimeters.
- Therefore, the total distance traveled in 150 revolutions is \( 150 \times 20\pi = 3000\pi \) centimeters.

Thus, the distance traveled by the point after 30 seconds is \( 3000\pi \) centimeters.

How many different codes can be made? # Answer option: ['A)1,980', 'B)2,020', 'C)2,100', 'D)2,200', 'E)1,900']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of different 3-letter codes that can be formed under the given conditions:

1. The middle letter must be a vowel.
2. The first and third letters must be different consonants.

Let's break down the steps:

1. **Choose the middle letter (vowel):**
- There are 5 vowels available: A, E, I, O, U.
- So, there are 5 choices for the middle letter.

2. **Choose the first letter (consonant):**
- There are 20 consonants available.
- So, there are 20 choices for the first letter.

3. **Choose the third letter (consonant):**
- The third letter must be a consonant and different from the first letter.
- Since one consonant is already used for the first letter, there are \(20 - 1 = 19\) choices left for the third letter.

Now, we calculate the total number of different codes:

\[
\text{Total codes} = (\text{choices for first letter}) \times (\text{choices for middle letter}) \times (\text{choices for third letter})
\]

\[
\text{Total codes} = 20 \times 5 \times 19

\[
\text{Total codes} = 1900
\]

Thus, the total number of different codes that can be made is 1,900.

Question: Let A and B be independent events with P (A) = 0.2 and P(B) = 0.8. Find P(A/B)? # Answer option: ['A)0.2', 'B)0.4', 'C)0.6', 'D)1.2', 'E)1.5']
To find \( P(A/B) \), we need to understand the concept of conditional probability. The conditional probability \( P(A/B) \) is defined as the probability of event A occurring given that event B has occurred. The formula for conditional probability is:

\[
P(A/B) = \frac{P(A \cap B)}{P(B)}
\]

Since A and B are independent events, the probability of both A and B occurring, \( P(A \cap B) \), is the product of their individual probabilities:

\[
P(A \cap B) = P(A) \times P(B) = 0.2 \times 0.8 = 0.16
\]

Now, substitute the values into the formula for conditional probability:

\[
P(A/B) = \frac{P(A \cap B)}{P(B)} = \frac{0.16}{0.8} = 0.2
\]

Thus, the probability \( P(A/B) \) is 0.2.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a

If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day? # Answer option: ['A)80', 'B)120', 'C)240', 'D)320', 'E)360']
To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:

1. **Initial Inventory**: The store starts with 600 golf balls.

2. **Golf Balls Sold**: By the end of the day, the store sold 80% of its inventory.
- 80% of 600 is calculated as follows:
\[
0.8 \times 600 = 480
\]
So, the store sold 480 golf balls.

3. **Equal Number of Yellow and White Balls Sold**: The problem states that the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so, sold all of its white golf balls.

4. **All White Balls Sold**: Since all the white golf balls were sold, and they were sold in equal number to the yellow golf balls, the number of white golf balls sold is half of the total golf balls sold.
- Therefore, the number of white golf balls sold is:
\[
\frac{480}{2} = 240
\]

5. **Initial Number of White Golf Balls**: Since all white golf balls were sold, the store initially had 240 white golf balls.

6. **Initial Number of Yellow Golf Balls**: The total initial inventory was 600 golf balls. If 240 of these were white, then the number of yellow golf balls initially is:
\[
600 - 240 = 360
\]

Therefore, the store had 360 yellow golf balls at the beginning of the day.

Question: If the probability that Stock A will increase in value during the next month is 0.56, and the probability that Stock B will increase in value during the next month is 0.74. What is the greatest value for the probability that neither of these two events will occur? # Answer option: ['A)0.22', 'B)0.26', 'C)0.37', 'D)0.46', 'E)0.63']
To find the greatest value for the probability that neither Stock A nor Stock B will increase in value, we need to consider the probabilities of the complementary events.

1. **Complementary Probabilities:**
- The probability that Stock A will not increase is \(1 - 0.56 = 0.44\).
- The probability that Stock B will not increase is \(1 - 0.74 = 0.26\).

2. **Independence Assumption:**
- If we assume that the events are independent, the probability that neither Stock A nor Stock B will increase is the product of their complementary probabilities:
\[
P(\text{Neither A nor B}) = P(\text{Not A}) \times P(\text{Not B}) = 0.44 \times 0.26 = 0.1144
\]

3. **Greatest Value Consideration:**
- To find the greatest possible value for the probability that neither event occurs, we consider the scenario where the events are mutually exclusive. This means that if one event occurs, the other cannot, which maximizes the probability that neither occurs.
- In this case, the probability that neither event occurs is:
\[
P(\text{Neither A nor B}) = 1 - P(\text{A or B})
\]
- Using the formula for the union of two events:
\[
P(\text{A or B}) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A \text{ and } B)
\]
- To maximize \(P(\text{Neither A nor B})\), we minimize \(P(A \text{ and } B)\). The minimum value for \(P(A \text{ and } B)\) is 0 when the events are mutually exclusive.
- Therefore:
\[
P(\text{A or B}) = 0.56 + 0.74 - 0 = 1.30
\]
- Since probabilities cannot exceed 1, the maximum value for \(P(\text{A or B})\) is 1. Thus:
\[
P(\text{Neither A nor B}) = 1 - 1 = 0
\]

4. **Conclusion:**
- The greatest value for the probability that neither event occurs, considering realistic scenarios, is when the events are independent, which gives us 0.1144. However, this is not an option.
- The closest option that represents a realistic scenario is when the events are not mutually exclusive, and the probability of neither occurring is calculated as:
\[
P(\text{Neither A nor B}) = 1 - (0.56 + 0.74 - 0.56 \times 0.74) = 1 - 0.8144 = 0.1856
\]
- The closest answer option to this realistic scenario is 0.26.

Therefore, the greatest value for the probability that neither of these two events will occur, given the options, is \(\boxed{B}\).

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: In a class 1/16 of the students study math, 1/10 of the students study bio, 1/8 of the students study english. The total number of students is a 4 digit number. Find the diffrence between maximum number of students and minimum number of students. # Answer option: ['A)8880', 'B)8870', 'C)8890', 'D)7890', 'E)6780']
To solve this problem, we need to find the total number of students, \( N \), which is a 4-digit number. The fractions of students studying different subjects must result in whole numbers of students. Therefore, \( N \) must be a common multiple of the denominators of the fractions: 16, 10, and 8.

1. **Find the Least Common Multiple (LCM):**

- The prime factorization of 16 is \( 2^4 \).
- The prime factorization of 10 is \( 2 \times 5 \).
- The prime factorization of 8 is \( 2^3 \).

The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime number that appears in these factorizations:

- For 2, the highest power is \( 2^4 \).
- For 5, the highest power is \( 5^1 \).

Therefore, the LCM is \( 2^4 \times 5 = 16 \times 5 = 80 \).

2. **Determine the Range of \( N \):**

Since \( N \) is a 4-digit number, it must be between 1000 and 9999. We need to find the smallest and largest 4-digit numbers that are multiples of 80.

- **Minimum \( N \):**
- Divide 1000 by 80: \( 1000 \div 80 = 12.5 \).
- The smallest integer greater than 12.5 is 13.
- Therefore, the smallest 4-digit multiple of 80 is \( 13 \times 80 = 1040 \).

- **Maximum \( N \):**
- Divide 9999 by 80: \( 9999 \div 80 = 124.9875 \).
- The largest integer less than 124.9875 is 124.
- Therefore, the largest 4-digit multiple of 80 is \( 124 \times 80 = 9920 \).

3. **Calculate the Difference:**

The difference between the maximum and minimum number of students is:
\[
9920 - 1040 = 8880
\]

Thus, the difference between the maximum and minimum number of students is 8880.
