Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand? # Answer option: ['A)10/7', 'B)20/7', 'C)30/7', 'D)40/7', 'E)50/7']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how much of the original mixture should be removed and replaced with pure sand to achieve a mixture with equal quantities of sand and clay.

1. **Initial Composition:**
- The original mixture is 10 kg, containing 30% sand and 70% clay.
- This means there are 3 kg of sand and 7 kg of clay in the mixture.

2. **Desired Composition:**
- We want the final mixture to have equal quantities of sand and clay, i.e., 50% sand and 50% clay.

3. **Let x be the amount of the mixture removed and replaced with pure sand.**
- When x kg of the mixture is removed, it contains 0.3x kg of sand and 0.7x kg of clay.
- After removing x kg of the mixture, the remaining mixture is (10 - x) kg, which contains:
- Sand: \(3 - 0.3x\) kg
- Clay: \(7 - 0.7x\) kg

4. **Replace x kg of the mixture with x kg of pure sand:**
- The new amount of sand in the mixture becomes \(3 - 0.3x + x\) kg.
- The amount of clay remains \(7 - 0.7x\) kg.

5. **Set the sand and clay quantities equal:**
\[
3 - 0.3x + x = 7 - 0.7x
\]
Simplify the equation:
\[
3 + 0.7x = 7 - 0.7x
\]
\[
1.4x = 4
\]
\[
x = \frac{4}{1.4} = \frac{40}{14} = \frac{20}{7}
\]

Thus, the amount of the mixture that needs to be removed and replaced with pure sand is \(\frac{20}{7}\) kg.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: The nefarious bandit Hoopsmot decides to go in with his criminal partner Smolapon to purchase a number of senators. Hoopsmot contributes $16,000 to their bribery pool, and Smolapon contributes just $4,000. Their total allows them to influence 30 senators. How many senators of these can be considered Hoopsmot's? # Answer option: ['A)18', 'B)20', 'C)22', 'D)24', 'E)26']
To determine how many senators can be considered Hoopsmot's, we need to calculate the proportion of the total bribery pool contributed by Hoopsmot and apply that proportion to the total number of senators influenced.

1. **Calculate the total bribery pool:**
- Hoopsmot contributes $16,000.
- Smolapon contributes $4,000.
- Total bribery pool = $16,000 + $4,000 = $20,000.

2. **Calculate the proportion of the pool contributed by Hoopsmot:**
- Hoopsmot's contribution = $16,000.
- Proportion = Hoopsmot's contribution / Total bribery pool = $16,000 / $20,000 = 0.8.

3. **Apply this proportion to the total number of senators:**
- Total senators influenced = 30.
- Senators considered Hoopsmot's = 0.8 * 30 = 24.

Therefore, the number of senators that can be considered Hoopsmot's is 24.

Question: A two digit number exceeds the sum of the digits of that number by 18. If the digit at the unit's place is double the digit in the ten's place, what is the number? # Answer option: ['A)12', 'B)24', 'C)42', 'D)48', 'E)49']
To solve this problem, let's define the two-digit number as \(10a + b\), where \(a\) is the digit in the ten's place and \(b\) is the digit in the unit's place.

We are given two conditions:

1. The number exceeds the sum of its digits by 18:
\[
10a + b = a + b + 18
\]

2. The digit at the unit's place is double the digit in the ten's place:
\[
b = 2a
\]

Let's solve these equations step by step.

### Step 1: Simplify the first condition
From the first condition:
\[
10a + b = a + b + 18
\]
Subtract \(a + b\) from both sides:
\[
9a = 18
\]
Divide both sides by 9:
\[
a = 2
\]

### Step 2: Use the second condition
From the second condition:
\[
b = 2a
\]
Substitute \(a = 2\) into this equation:
\[
b = 2 \times 2 = 4
\]

### Step 3: Form the number
Now, substitute \(a = 2\) and \(b = 4\) back into the expression for the number:
\[
10a + b = 10 \times 2 + 4 = 20 + 4 = 24
\]

Thus, the two-digit number is 24.

### Step 4: Verify the conditions
- The sum of the digits is \(2 + 4 = 6\).
- The number 24 exceeds the sum of its digits by \(24 - 6 = 18\), which satisfies the first condition.
- The digit at the unit's place (4) is double the digit in the ten's place (2), which satisfies the second condition.

Therefore, the correct answer is \(\boxed{24}\).

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b

Add 17 to both sides:

\[ ? \times 19 = 95 \]

Divide both sides by 19 to solve for "?":

Calculate the division:

Question: Two cars are travelling from the same starting point in the same direction, having started their commute at the same time. The first car travels at a steady rate of 55 mph, while the second travels at a steady rate of 52 mph. How much time will pass before the cars are 15 miles away from each other? # Answer option: ['A)3 hours', 'B)5 hours', 'C)6 hours', 'D)4 hours', 'E)7 hours']
To determine how much time will pass before the two cars are 15 miles apart, we need to consider their relative speeds. The first car is traveling at 55 mph, and the second car is traveling at 52 mph. The difference in their speeds is:

\[ 55 \text{ mph} - 52 \text{ mph} = 3 \text{ mph} \]

This means that the first car is moving away from the second car at a rate of 3 miles per hour.

We want to find out how long it will take for the distance between the two cars to be 15 miles. Since the relative speed between the two cars is 3 mph, we can set up the equation:

\[ \text{Time} = \frac{\text{Distance}}{\text{Relative Speed}} = \frac{15 \text{ miles}}{3 \text{ mph}} \]

Calculating this gives:

\[ \text{Time} = 5 \text{ hours} \]

Therefore, it will take 5 hours for the two cars to be 15 miles apart.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: If a subscription for 15 issues of a magazine costs $42.00 and represents a saving of 25 percent of the cover prices, what is the cover price per issue? # Answer option: ['A)$7.73', 'B)$6.73', 'C)$5.73', 'D)$4.73', 'E)$3.73']
To find the cover price per issue, we need to determine the total cover price for 15 issues and then divide by 15 to find the price per issue.

1. **Understand the savings**: The subscription cost of $42.00 represents a 25% savings off the total cover price. This means that the subscription cost is 75% of the total cover price.

2. **Set up the equation**: Let \( x \) be the total cover price for 15 issues. Since $42.00 is 75% of the total cover price, we can write the equation:
\[
0.75x = 42
\]

3. **Solve for \( x \)**: Divide both sides of the equation by 0.75 to find the total cover price.
\[
x = \frac{42}{0.75} = 56
\]

4. **Find the cover price per issue**: Now that we know the total cover price for 15 issues is $56, we divide by 15 to find the cover price per issue.
\[
\text{Cover price per issue} = \frac{56}{15} \approx 3.73
\]

5. **Select the correct answer**: The cover price per issue is approximately $3.73, which corresponds to option E.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: The greatest common factor of two positive integers is 11. The least common multiple of these two integers is 7700. If one of the integers is 350, what is the other? # Answer option: ['A)242', 'B)308', 'C)352', 'D)412', 'E)456']
To solve this problem, we need to use the relationship between the greatest common factor (GCF), the least common multiple (LCM), and the two integers. The relationship is given by:

\[
\text{GCF}(a, b) \times \text{LCM}(a, b) = a \times b
\]

We are given:
- GCF = 11
- LCM = 7700
- One of the integers, \( a = 350 \)

We need to find the other integer, \( b \).

First, substitute the known values into the equation:

\[
11 \times 7700 = 350 \times b
\]

Calculate the left side:

\[
11 \times 7700 = 84700
\]

Now, solve for \( b \):

\[
84700 = 350 \times b
\]

Divide both sides by 350 to isolate \( b \):

\[
b = \frac{84700}{350}
\]

Calculate the division:

\[
b = 242
\]

Thus, the other integer is 242. Let's verify that this solution satisfies the conditions:

1. Check the GCF of 350 and 242:
- The prime factorization of 350 is \( 2 \times 5^2 \times 7 \).
- The prime factorization of 242 is \( 2 \times 11^2 \).

The only common factor is 11, which matches the given GCF.

2. Check the LCM of 350 and 242:
- The LCM is calculated by taking the highest power of all prime factors present in either number.
- LCM = \( 2^1 \times 5^2 \times 7^1 \times 11^2 = 7700 \), which matches the given LCM.

Both conditions are satisfied, confirming that the other integer is indeed 242.

Final answer: \(\{A\}\)
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: Shweta rides at the rate of 10 km per hour but stops for 10 minutes to take rest at the end of every 15 km. How many hours will she take to cover 100 km # Answer option: ['A)9 hours.', 'B)10 hours.', 'C)11 hours.', 'D)12 hours.', 'E)13 hours.']
To determine how long it will take Shweta to cover 100 km, we need to consider both her riding speed and her rest breaks.

1. **Calculate the time taken to ride 15 km:**
- Shweta rides at 10 km per hour.
- Time to ride 15 km = Distance / Speed = 15 km / 10 km per hour = 1.5 hours.

2. **Calculate the number of 15 km segments in 100 km:**
- 100 km / 15 km per segment = 6 full segments with a remainder.
- 6 segments cover 90 km, leaving 10 km remaining.

3. **Calculate the total riding time for 90 km:**
- Each 15 km segment takes 1.5 hours.
- For 6 segments: 6 segments × 1.5 hours per segment = 9 hours.

4. **Calculate the rest time for 90 km:**
- Shweta rests for 10 minutes (or 1/6 of an hour) at the end of each 15 km segment.
- She will rest 5 times for the first 90 km (since she doesn't rest after the last segment if she finishes her journey).
- Total rest time = 5 rests × 1/6 hour per rest = 5/6 hours.

5. **Calculate the time to ride the remaining 10 km:**
- Time to ride 10 km = Distance / Speed = 10 km / 10 km per hour = 1 hour.

6. **Add up all the times:**
- Total riding time = 9 hours (for 90 km) + 1 hour (for the remaining 10 km) = 10 hours.
- Total rest time = 5/6 hours.

7. **Total time taken:**
- Total time = Total riding time + Total rest time = 10 hours + 5/6 hours = 10 + 0.8333 hours ≈ 10.8333 hours.

Since the options are in whole hours, we round 10.8333 hours to the nearest whole number, which is 11 hours.

Final answer: {C}
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: When folded into two equal halves a rectangular sheet had a perimeter of 48cm for each part folded along one set of sides and the same is 66cm when folded along the other set of sides. Find the area of the sheet. # Answer option: ['A)1584', 'B)1120', 'C)792', 'D)1320', 'E)1200']
To solve this problem, we need to find the dimensions of the original rectangular sheet and then calculate its area.

Let's denote the length and width of the original rectangular sheet as \( L \) and \( W \), respectively.

1. **Folding along one set of sides:**

When the sheet is folded along one set of sides, the perimeter of each part is 48 cm. This means that the folded dimension is half of one of the original dimensions. Let's assume the sheet is folded along its length \( L \), so each part has dimensions \( \frac{L}{2} \) and \( W \).

The perimeter of each folded part is given by:
\[
2 \left( \frac{L}{2} + W \right) = 48
\]
Simplifying, we get:
\[
L + 2W = 48 \quad \text{(Equation 1)}
\]

2. **Folding along the other set of sides:**

When the sheet is folded along the other set of sides, the perimeter of each part is 66 cm. This means the sheet is folded along its width \( W \), so each part has dimensions \( L \) and \( \frac{W}{2} \).

The perimeter of each folded part is given by:
\[
2 \left( L + \frac{W}{2} \right) = 66
\]
Simplifying, we get:
\[
2L + W = 66 \quad \text{(Equation 2)}
\]

3. **Solving the system of equations:**

We have the following system of equations:
\[
L + 2W = 48
\]
\[
2L + W = 66
\]

To solve for \( L \) and \( W \), we can multiply Equation 1 by 2:
\[
2L + 4W = 96
\]

Now, subtract Equation 2 from this result:
\[
(2L + 4W) - (2L + W) = 96 - 66
\]
\[
3W = 30
\]
\[
W = 10
\]

Substitute \( W = 10 \) back into Equation 1:
\[
L + 2(10) = 48
\]
\[
L + 20 = 48
\]
\[
L = 28
\]

4. **Calculating the area:**

The area of the original rectangular sheet is:
\[
\text{Area} = L \times W = 28 \times 10 = 280
\]

It seems there was a mistake in the calculation. Let's re-evaluate the equations and calculations:

Re-evaluate the system of equations:
- \( L + 2W = 48 \)
- \( 2L + W = 66 \)

Substitute \( W = 10 \) into the correct equation:
- \( L + 2(10) = 48 \)
- \( L + 20 = 48 \)
- \( L = 28 \)

Re-calculate the area:
- \( \text{Area} = L \times W = 28 \times 10 = 280 \)

It seems there was a mistake in the options provided. The correct area based on the calculations is 280, which is not listed in the options. Please verify the problem statement and options.
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: When I was 2 years old, my brother was half my age. Now I am 60 years old, how old is my brother? # Answer option: ['A)A)59', 'B)B)69', 'C)C)79', 'D)D)89', 'E)E)99']
To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:

1. **Initial Age Difference**: When you were 2 years old, your brother was half your age. This means your brother was 1 year old at that time. Therefore, the age difference between you and your brother is 1 year.

2. **Current Age**: You are now 60 years old.

3. **Brother's Current Age**: Since the age difference between you and your brother is 1 year, and you are 60 years old, your brother is 1 year younger than you. Therefore, your brother is 60 - 1 = 59 years old.

Thus, the correct answer is:

Final answer: {A}

Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y. # Answer option: ['A)144km', 'B)72 km', 'C)126km', 'D)84 km', 'E)48km']
To solve this problem, we need to analyze the movements of Allen and Bob and determine the distance between X and Y.

1. **Define Variables:**
- Let the distance between X and Y be \( d \) km.
- Allen's speed is 54 km/h.
- Bob's speed is 78 km/h.

2. **First Meeting:**
- Allen and Bob start at the same time and move towards each other.
- Their relative speed is \( 54 + 78 = 132 \) km/h.
- They will meet for the first time after covering the entire distance \( d \).
- Time taken for the first meeting is \( \frac{d}{132} \) hours.

3. **Second Meeting:**
- After the first meeting, Allen continues to Y and Bob continues to X.
- Once they reach their respective destinations, they turn around and head back.
- They meet for the second time after Bob has covered 48 km more than Allen.

4. **Distance Covered by Bob and Allen:**
- Let the time taken from the start until the second meeting be \( t \) hours.
- Distance covered by Bob in time \( t \) is \( 78t \) km.
- Distance covered by Allen in time \( t \) is \( 54t \) km.
- According to the problem, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the second meeting:
\[
78t = 54t + 48
\]
- Solving for \( t \):
\[
78t - 54t = 48 \\
24t = 48 \\
t = 2 \text{ hours}
\]

5. **Calculate Distance \( d \):**
- In 2 hours, the total distance covered by both Allen and Bob together is:
\[
78t + 54t = 132t = 132 \times 2 = 264 \text{ km}
\]
- Since they meet twice, the total distance covered is twice the distance between X and Y:
\[
2d = 264 \\
d = 132 \text{ km}
\]

6. **Conclusion:**
- The distance between X and Y is 132 km.

Therefore, the final answer is: \(\text{Final answer: \{C\}}\)
Final Answer:
Ground Truth Answer: e
